Tides throughout human history Coastal
Community and Maritime civilizations
have tuned in to the tides the twice
daily rise and fall of the sea
Babylonian and Greek astronomers
recognized the relationship between the
Tide's height and the moon's position in
its
orbit they believed that almost the same
spiritual forces that governed the
Motions of the planets connected
them early Arabic astronomers believed
sea temperature fluctuations influenced
tides seeking support for heliocentrism
Galileo proposed that Tides come from
the sloshing of the oceans during the
Earth's motion around the Sun the
English mathematician physicist and
astronomer Isaac Newton was the first to
propose the correct origin of the tides
linking the Earth Moon and Sun among
other things Newton had been working on
a generalized Theory to explain Kepler's
laws of planetary motion and by 1686 he
had developed the basic outline for new
theories of Universal gravity and laws
of motion Newton hypothesized that both
the moon and the sun exert a strong
gravitational attraction on the earth
and vice versa since verified and
enhanced by Space Age observations his
breakthrough Discovery was that
gravitational forces alone not the
Earth's spin or orbital motion acting on
the Earth's thin fluid ocean shell are
almost entirely responsible for the
tides the moon's gravitational raction
raises a deep water ocean tide of about
20 in 50
cm the sun's tidal effect is about half
that in shallow water tidal Heights can
be up to 10 times larger and the tides
at any particular coastal location are a
strong function of the positions of the
Sun and Moon as well as the local seaf
FL depth and Coastline
shape the Earth's and Moon's solid parts
also bulge in response to gravitational
tidal attraction
with an amplitude typically about half
that of the oceanic Tides solid and
liquid deformation dissipates energy in
the Earth Moon system through tidal
friction as a result the earth spin is
slowing down by a few milliseconds per
century and the Moon is slowly receding
from the Earth by about 13 ft 4 m per
Century Sir Isaac Newton asserts that
there is a gravitational connection
between the Moon Earth and Sun each
exerts strong gravitational attractive
forces on the other in proportion to
their masses and inversely proportional
to the square of their
distances the fluid nature of Earth's
oceans allows these forces to express
themselves as
Tides Newton's laws of gravity and
motion the Scientific Revolution began

objects one in an essentially circular

other Celestial mechanicians built upon
lr's Discovery to address more
comprehensive three-body problems

and asteroids ring particles or even
grains of cosmic dust to comprehend
elucidate and forecast intricate motions
within our solar system discovery of

spectroscopy Isaac Newton's experiments
in 1672 demonstrated that sunlight is
not white or yellow but rather a
spectrum of Many Colors that refract
slightly differently when passing
through an object like a prism others
including fellow English scientist
William Hyde walliston widely repeated

Spectrum in

use this specially designed prism could

lines with his spectroscope he observed

Suns by the mid 19th century physicists

parallax Parallax is an object's

finger will appear to move because of
the small change in viewing

Parallax it is possible to do a similar

us from aristarchus's time to tyos

Doppler shift of
light most of us are familiar with the
dramatic change in the sound of an
ambulance train whistle or race car as
it approaches us and then speeds past as
the vehicle recedes its sound changes to
a distinctly lower pitch or frequency
than when it was
approaching this change is known as the
Doppler effect named after the Austrian
physicist Christian Doppler who first
proposed in 1842 that the observed
frequency of any wave should depend on
the relative difference in speeds
between the wave source and the obs OB
erver in 1845 Dutch meteorologist CHD by
ballot cleverly verified doppler's
hypothesis for sound waves by hiring
musicians to play notes on a moving
train and then having stationary
observers report the pitches they heard
as the musicians approached and
receded in 1848 the French physicist
Armon iolite fizo showed how doppler's
hypothesis applied to light waves by
noting slight changes in frequency or
shifts of absorption lines in the
Spectra of
stars according to astronomers the size
and direction of these frequency changes
known as Doppler shifts can reveal the
speed at which astronomical bodies are
approaching or receding from one
another objects approaching us have
their Spectra shifted to higher
frequencies or shorter Bluer wavelengths
conversely objects receding from us have
their Spectra shifted to red
in the 1860s we measured the first
accurate relative Stellar velocities and
in the 1870s we detected the Stars
Doppler shift due to the Earth's annual
motion around the Sun in the early 20th
century the American astronomer vesto
slier observed that most of the known
nebuli such as those in messier's list
were red shifted or moving away from us
soon after Edwin Hubble another American
showed that many of these nebuli were
other galaxies enormously far from the
Milky
Way Hubble's work led directly to the
concept of an expanding universe and the
Big Bang Theory
Hyperion William Hershel's discovery of
MERS in 1789 led to the discovery of no
new moons around Jupiter Saturn or
Uranus for more than 50 years still in
late 1848 the two groups independently
discovered Saturn's eighth known
satellite within days of each
other the American Father and Son
astronomer team of William Bond and
George Bond observed the new moon
first still the English astronomer
William lassle was the first to announce
his
observations all three astronomers were
credited with the
discovery just one year earlier John
hsel published a compendium of new
observations in which he proposed a
Greek Titan naming scheme for the moons
of Saturn cell endorsed the scheme and
suggested that the newest moon be named
Hyperion after the Greek Titan and
brother of cronis the Greek equivalent
Saturn little was known about Hyperion
except that it traveled in a relatively
eccentric orbit at an average distance
of about 25 times the radius of Saturn
well outside the planet's ring system
until the Voyager flybys in the 1980s
and then the Cassini Saturn orbit
emissions encounters with the moon in
the early 2000s
Hyperion is the first and largest
irregular non-spherical moon discovered
by a
telescope space mission images show it
to be an elongated body and more recent
telescope spectroscopy shows it to have
a surface composed of dark reddish dirty
water ice perhaps similar to that on the
dark side of
iapetus Hyperion has a weird spongy
surface characterized by tons of deep
impact craters sharp edged pits and
cliffs a giant impact crater 75 m 120 km
wide and 6 M 10 km deep scars one whole
side of the
moon this suggests that Hyperion is only
a fragment of a larger satellite broken
apart by a giant

an observer on Earth's surface would
perceive such a satellite as stationary
parked high in the sky Newton's Second
Law uses the Earth's mass and rotation
rate to calculate the orbital altitude

it to be approximately 22,000 M 36,000
km above the surface the British science

help us monitor Earth's weather and

environment gravitational
lensing the curvature of space and time
near extremely massive objects is a
fundamental feature of physicist Albert
Einstein's early 20th century theory of
general
relativity Einstein and others predicted
that due to the curvature of SpaceTime
the gravitational field of massive
foreground objects would bend light from
distant
objects Arthur Stanley Edington a
British astrophysicist confirmed the
prediction in 19 19 when he noticed that
stars observed near the Sun during a
solar eclipse were slightly out of
position Einstein continued to study
this effect in the
1930s and he and others including the
Swiss American astronomer Fritz zwicki
speculated that more massive objects
such as galaxies and clusters of
galaxies could Bend and amplify light
from distant objects almost as a lens
bends and magnifies normal light however
however it took many decades for
astronomers to find observational
evidence of such gravitational
lensing in
1979 astronomers at the kit Peak
National observatory in Arizona
discovered the first example of what
appeared to be Twin
quers Two active Galactic nuclei very
close to each other in the
sky a foreground Galaxy's strong
gravitational field bent and split the
light of the two quers into two parts
since then researchers have discovered
numerous additional examples of
gravitational lensing suggesting three
possible mechanisms for the effect to
occur strong lensing occurs when
distinct multiple or partial usually
arike images are
formed weak lensing has been detectable
by observing small and subtle shifts in
star or Galaxy positions over large
regions in micr lensing events the
gravitational lensing effect of a large
foreground Mass such as another star or
Galaxy temporarily amplifies the
brightness of random distant stars or
even
planets initially researchers discovered
and studied gravitational lenses as
accidental serendipitous
events however scientists have
intentionally conducted several
astronomical surveys to search for
gravitational lensing
events these surveys aim to obtain
unique measur ments of the properties of
distant galaxies that would not be
visible without the lens amplification
as well as the properties such as mass

when physicist Albert Einstein developed
his theory of general relativity early
in the 20th century to explain the
relationship between space time and
matter in the presence of gravitational
fields it was in the context of what
astronomers believed at the time to be a
static or unchanging
Universe to make his theory work
Einstein had to invent an as yet unseen
Force which he called the cosm logical
constant to counteract the attractive
force of gravity and enable the universe
to remain
static in 1929 Edwin Hubble's discovery
of space expansion LED Einstein to
conclude that his cosmological constant
was no longer
necessary everything fit
nicely but astronomers detailed study of
spiral galaxies and Galactic cluster
motions over subsequent decades led to
the surprising discovery of an unseen
but gravitationally attractive material
known as dark matter as well as The
Humbling realization that most of the
universe consists of matter that we
cannot observe
directly even more surprising was the
discovery by astronomers in
1998 that the universe's expansion
appears to be accelerating with time
that is galaxies nearer to us which we
observe in the relatively modern era of
the universe are moving away from each
other faster than extremely distant
galaxies which we observe from much
earlier in the universe's history one
possible explanation is that some unseen
energy force or pressure permeates the
vacuum of space and acts opposite to
gravity helping to accelerate the normal
expansion of space since the Big
Bang cosmologists call this hypothesized
Force Dark
Energy maybe Einstein was right about
his cosmological constant after all dark
Energy's true nature or existence is
impossible to study directly with
traditional telescopic
observations similar to dark matter we
can only indirectly infer its Presence
by studying its gravitational effects on
normal
matter if Dark Energy proves to be real
however it would lead to an even more
stunning and humbling realization about
our
universe dark energy and dark matter
things we currently have no way to
measure or car ciz comprise 96% of the
energy in our universe while ordinary
matter galaxies stars planets and US
account for only 4% of the cosmos Torino

evidence for all but a few hundred
terrestrial impact craters but the

altered the planet's climate and

exponentially still even in modern times

Planetary Exploration the solar neutrino
problem the so-called standard model of
20th century physics provides a theory
that connects matter and energy through
the interactions of Elementary particles
forces familiar elements of the standard
model include the electron a fundamental
particle of charge and the photon a
fundamental particle of
light the neutrons Discovery in 1933
led to the neutrinos prediction and
Discovery in
1956 this led to the hypothesis that
neutrinos like photons are massless
Elementary particles that travel at the
speed of light creating three flavors
electron muon and to neutrinos depending
on the process and
environment neutrino astronomy became an
active way to probe high energy
processes in inaccessible places like
the sun's interior
large neutrino detectors started coming
online in the 1960s to detect elusive
neutrino particles generated in the Sun
or during high energy Cosmic events such
as Supernova
explosions according to the standard
model hydrogen fusion with helium inside
the sun should create electron neutrinos
that these detectors could find in fact
these detectors discovered the predicted
solar neutrinos but at a rate only about
1/3 of what the model predicted
the missing neutrinos created what
particle physicists called the solar
neutrino problem physicists made solving
the solar neutrino problem a top
priority because the standard model
might only be accurate if they could
theorists wondered if neutrinos could
change flavors or oscillate between
their different
types in the 1990s researchers built new
higher resolution detector experiments
to improve measurement Fidelity and in
2001 one the new data revealed a
surprising Revelation neutrinos are not
massless particles they possess
extremely small masses and move
marginally slower than light most
importantly experiments showed that they
can oscillate between electron muon and
Tow flavors and about 2/3 of the
electron neutrinos created inside the
sun eventually convert to other
flavors solving the solar neutrino
problem led to Raymond Davis Jr and
masatoshi kiba's 2002 Nobel Prize in
physics more importantly it led to
critical revisions of the standard model
which now accounts for oscillations by
neutrons and other
particles age of the
universe we built the Hubble Space
Telescope HST as a Time Machine by
gazing deeper into space it also peers
farther back in time detecting light
emitted by stars and galaxies billions
of years ago using standard candles such
as sephi variable stars or certain types
of supernova explosions in Far distant
galaxies astronomers have been able to
use HST to refine Hubble's Law and to
determine the rate of the expansion of
cosmos after a decade of observations in
2001 HST scientists announced that by
turning the clock backward on their
derived expansion rate they could deduce
that the Big Bang had occurred
approximately 13.7 billion years ago at
the same time scientists launched a new

wmm the satellite T Wilkinson took

anisotropies in the 3 Kelvin background

few hundred, years after the big bang at
the beginning of the so-called Dark Ages
but before the birth of the first Stars

methods the W map data led to an

billion

13.75 plus 0.11 billion years ago a

wind the sun like all stars is powered
by the dynamic balance between the
gravitational contraction of an enormous
Mass concentration and the outward
pressure of intense nuclear fusion
reactions occurring in its deep
interior the sun emits radiation that
provides heat and light to the planets
but its Photosphere and chromosphere
also release highly energetic particles
into interplanetary space at high
speeds we refer to this stream of
particles as the solar wind in 1995 the
European Space Agency Esa and NASA
teamed up to launch a satellite called
the solar and heliospheric Observatory
Soho we specifically designed this
satellite to study the sun's Dynamic
environment including the solar wind
using high resolution ultraviolet images
spectroscopy Soho continues to provide
spectacular time-lapse views of our
Dynamic
star solar astronomers discoveries about
the solar wind from Soho and other
studies generated substantial interest
in a dedicated space mission to collect

sun planetary scientists too are keenly

it represents about
99.9% of the Solar System's mass and is

formed NASA designed the Genesis mission

until early

work inside the Sun and other stars
